###begin p 59
###xml 42 47 42 47 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rad59</italic>
###xml 125 134 125 130 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rad1&#916;</italic>
###xml 148 149 144 145 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig8" ref-type="fig">8</xref>
###xml 156 166 152 162 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rad59-Y92A</italic>
###xml 228 269 224 257 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rad1&#916;/rad1&#916; rad59-Y92A/rad59-Y92A</italic>
###xml 336 355 324 335 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rad1&#916;/rad1&#916;</italic>
###xml 419 460 399 424 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rad1&#916;/rad1&#916; rad59&#916;/rad59&#916;</italic>
###xml 484 495 448 459 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rad59-K166A</italic>
###xml 576 607 540 563 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rad1&#916;/rad1&#916; rad59-K166A</italic>
###xml 608 619 564 575 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rad59-K166A</italic>
###xml 784 789 740 745 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rad59</italic>
###xml 833 842 789 794 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rad1&#916;</italic>
###xml 857 876 809 820 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rad1&#916;/rad1&#916;</italic>
###xml 876 887 820 831 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rad59/rad59</italic>
###xml 1009 1028 953 964 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rad1&#916;/rad1&#916;</italic>
###xml 1159 1200 1095 1120 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rad1&#916;/rad1&#916; rad59&#916;/rad59&#916;</italic>
###xml 1275 1280 1195 1200 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rad59</italic>
###xml 1347 1351 1267 1271 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">RAD1</italic>
###xml 1367 1377 1287 1293 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rad59&#916;</italic>
When the 311 bp substrates were used, the rad59 missense alleles displayed variable capacities to suppress the effect of the rad1Delta allele (Fig. 8). The rad59-Y92A allele suppressed least, raising translocation levels in the rad1Delta/rad1Delta rad59-Y92A/rad59-Y92A double homozygote approximately 10-fold from that observed in the rad1Delta/rad1Delta homozygote, which is very similar to the level observed in the rad1Delta/rad1Delta rad59Delta/rad59Delta double homozygote. The rad59-K166A allele suppressed most, with translocation frequencies increased 50-fold in the rad1Delta/rad1Delta rad59-K166A/rad59-K166A double homozygote. Shortening the amount of homology available for recombination to 60 bp, had the effect of nearly erasing the differences in the abilities of the rad59 missense alleles to suppress the effect of rad1Delta, as all three rad1Delta/rad1Deltarad59/rad59 double homozygotes displayed translocation frequencies that were between 7- and 13-fold higher than that observed in the rad1Delta/rad1Delta homozygote. Notably, the translocation frequencies for all three of these double homozygotes were significantly below that of the rad1Delta/rad1Delta rad59Delta/rad59Delta double homozygote, indicating that with the short substrates, none of the rad59 missense alleles were capable of suppressing the effect of losing RAD1 as well as the rad59Delta null allele.
###end p 59
###begin title 60
Discussion
###end title 60
###begin p 61
###xml 21 26 21 26 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">RAD59</italic>
###xml 233 237 233 237 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR2">1996</xref>
###xml 258 262 258 262 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR14">1999</xref>
###xml 280 284 280 284 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR46">2000</xref>
###xml 298 302 298 302 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR9">2007</xref>
###xml 527 528 527 528 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig4" ref-type="fig">4</xref>
###xml 530 531 530 531 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig5" ref-type="fig">5</xref>
###xml 591 592 591 592 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Tab2" ref-type="table">2</xref>
###xml 600 601 600 601 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig6" ref-type="fig">6</xref>
###xml 603 604 603 604 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig7" ref-type="fig">7</xref>
###xml 900 904 900 904 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR1">2008</xref>
###xml 1002 1006 1002 1006 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR51">2006</xref>
###xml 1072 1077 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
Since its discovery, RAD59 has been implicated in various types of intrachromosomal mitotic recombination events involving inverted or direct repeats while exhibiting limited effects on heteroallelic recombination (Bai and Symington 1996; Jablonovich et al. 1999; Sugawara et al. 2000; Feng et al. 2007). This implicates Rad59 as a major component of SSA, but dispensable for other types of HR. Our current results confirm these findings, as Rad59 was found to be essential for efficient inter- and intrachromosomal SSA (Figs. 4, 5), but to contribute little to other types of events (Table 2; Figs. 6, 7). The relevance of SSA to eukaryotic genome stability is clearly implied when one considers that translocation formation by recombination between repetitive elements is a major consequence of acute radiation exposure, which results in the creation of hundreds of DSBs per genome (Argueso et al. 2008), and that these processes are likely to be recapitulated in higher eukaryotes (Weinstock et al. 2006). Therefore, developing an understanding of the role of Rad59 in yeast SSA may provide greater insight into how genome stability is controlled in higher systems.
###end p 61
###begin p 62
###xml 66 71 66 71 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">RAD59</italic>
###xml 880 884 854 858 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR15">2002</xref>
###xml 898 903 872 877 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rad59</italic>
###xml 503 508 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 1067 1072 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 1077 1082 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
This study presents the characterization of four novel alleles of RAD59, three of which were found to lead to partial defects in translocation formation by SSA. These alleles bear mutations that alter amino acids conserved between Rad59 and Rad52. Information regarding the roles played by these amino acids in the function of Rad52, both in vivo and in vitro, suggests ways in which changing the analogous amino acids affect the function of Rad59. The crystal structure of the first 212 amino acids of human Rad52 reveals a monomer with a putative DNA-binding groove and a protrusion consisting of a beta-beta-beta-alpha-fold. Following assembly into an undecamer complex, the beta-beta-beta-alpha structure forms a round "stem" base and the binding groove creates a "domed-cap" with a positively charged channel running along the upper surface to accommodate DNA (Kagawa et al. 2002). All of the rad59 mutants created in this study fall within the region that creates the beta-beta-beta-alpha motif, which is the most highly conserved region between Rad59 and both yeast and human Rad52.
###end p 62
###begin p 63
###xml 80 82 67 69 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Hs</italic>
###xml 221 225 208 212 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR15">2002</xref>
###xml 328 338 315 325 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rad59-Y92A</italic>
###xml 506 508 493 495 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Hs</italic>
###xml 645 647 632 634 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Hs</italic>
###xml 667 671 654 658 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR22">2005</xref>
###xml 770 772 757 759 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Hs</italic>
###xml 978 988 965 975 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rad59-Y92A</italic>
###xml 1039 1049 1026 1036 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rad52-Y96A</italic>
###xml 1075 1079 1062 1066 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR29">2002</xref>
###xml 1096 1100 1083 1087 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR18">2006</xref>
###xml 862 867 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 872 877 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 1033 1038 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
Tyr92 of Rad59 lies at the very beginning of the beta-beta-beta-alpha motif. In HsRad52, the analogous Tyr81 protrudes from the monomer and fits into a hydrophobic pocket created on the neighboring monomer (Kagawa et al. 2002), indicating that this residue is important for quaternary structure. Therefore, the phenotype of the rad59-Y92A mutant may be due to a defect in its ability to associate with other Rad59 monomers, Rad52, or perhaps other SSA factors. Experiments performed in vitro with purified HsRad52 demonstrate that mutation of Tyr81 inhibits oligomerization of the C-terminally truncated (1-212) protein, but not the full-length HsRad52 (Lloyd et al. 2005). This suggests that Tyr92 of Rad59, which is of similar dimensions as the C-terminally truncated HsRad52, may play a more important role in protein-protein interactions than in full length yeast and human Rad52, and may explain why we observed a somewhat more severe recombination defect conferred by the rad59-Y92A allele than that conferred by the analogous yeast rad52-Y96A allele (Mortensen et al. 2002; Lettier et al. 2006).
###end p 63
###begin p 64
###xml 269 271 252 254 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Hs</italic>
###xml 411 415 394 398 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR15">2002</xref>
###xml 430 434 413 417 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR22">2005</xref>
###xml 658 660 641 643 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Sc</italic>
###xml 697 699 680 682 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Hs</italic>
###xml 777 778 760 761 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig4" ref-type="fig">4</xref>
###xml 780 781 763 764 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig5" ref-type="fig">5</xref>
###xml 800 804 783 787 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR29">2002</xref>
###xml 1318 1329 1297 1308 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rad59-K166A</italic>
###xml 1334 1345 1313 1324 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rad59-F180A</italic>
###xml 1423 1428 1402 1407 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">RAD52</italic>
###xml 1435 1446 1414 1425 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rad52-K159A</italic>
###xml 1451 1462 1430 1441 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rad52-F173A</italic>
###xml 1529 1533 1508 1512 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR29">2002</xref>
###xml 1729 1730 1708 1709 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig3" ref-type="fig">3</xref>
###xml 891 896 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 952 957 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 1417 1422 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
Mutation of the Lys166 and Phe180 residues of Rad59 resulted in the largest effects in our analysis, and both of these residues lie in the alpha-helix of the putative beta-beta-beta-alpha motif. While the impact of the analogous mutations in the C-terminally truncated HsRad52 has not been reported, mutation of Lys152, which is also present in this helix, displays a clear defect in DNA binding (Kagawa et al. 2002; Lloyd et al. 2005), indicating that residues within the corresponding Rad59 helix, especially the positively charged Lys166, may be directly involved in physically contacting the DNA. Interestingly, mutation of Lys174 of Rad59 and Lys167 of ScRad52, which correspond to Lys152 of HsRad52, have not been observed to result in any effect on recombination (Figs. 4, 5; Mortensen et al. 2002). These results suggest that either this lysine is not involved in DNA binding by the yeast proteins or that DNA binding within this region of the yeast Rad52 and Rad59 proteins is not essential for recombination in vivo. Alternatively, slight variations in the amino acid sequence between Rad52 and Rad59 could result in this residue being on a turn of the alpha helix that does not allow for interaction. While these data make it difficult to predict which biochemical function of Rad59 may be disrupted by the rad59-K166A and rad59-F180A mutations, it is important to note that the analogous mutations in the yeast RAD52 gene, rad52-K159A and rad52-F173A, confer quite significant recombination defects (Mortensen et al. 2002), suggesting that these conserved residues are important for the proper function of both proteins in HR. The relatively minor effects of these mutations on the steady state levels of Rad59 (Fig. 3) suggest that their effects on recombination are more likely due to defects in a conserved biochemical function than reduced levels of protein.
###end p 64
###begin p 65
###xml 156 160 156 160 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR10">1992</xref>
###xml 246 250 246 250 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR33">1999</xref>
###xml 349 353 349 353 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR46">2000</xref>
###xml 372 376 372 376 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR32">2008</xref>
###xml 397 401 397 401 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR23">2009</xref>
###xml 706 707 706 707 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig8" ref-type="fig">8</xref>
###xml 726 730 726 730 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR32">2008</xref>
###xml 776 817 776 801 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rad52&#916;/rad52&#916; rad1&#916;/rad1&#916;</italic>
###xml 906 925 890 901 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rad1&#916;/rad1&#916;</italic>
###xml 1015 1024 991 996 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rad1&#916;</italic>
###xml 1045 1055 1017 1023 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rad59&#916;</italic>
###xml 1081 1085 1049 1053 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR32">2008</xref>
###xml 1152 1157 1120 1125 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rad59</italic>
###xml 1179 1188 1147 1152 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rad1&#916;</italic>
The Rad1-Rad10 nuclease is required to remove non-homologous DNA tails from annealed intermediates in the penultimate step of SSA (Fishman-Lobell and Haber 1992). While Rad59 demonstrates the ability to anneal complementary DNA (Petukhova et al. 1999), it has also been suggested that it participates in non-homologous tail removal (Sugawara et al. 2000; Pannunzio et al. 2008; Lyndaker and Alani 2009). Previously, we had shown that simultaneous loss of Rad1 and Rad59 resulted in levels of translocation formation by SSA that could substantially exceed those observed when either one alone was removed, suggesting that both suppress an alternative mechanism for removal of the non-homologous tails (Fig. 8; Pannunzio et al. 2008). This was distinct from results measured in rad52Delta/rad52Delta rad1Delta/rad1Delta double homozygotes, where translocation frequency remained at the level observed in the rad1Delta/rad1Delta single homozygotes, indicating that suppression of the translocation defect conferred by rad1Delta was specific to the rad59Delta allele (Pannunzio et al. 2008). Therefore, by examining the epistasis relationships between the rad59 missense alleles and rad1Delta, we were able to further reveal a function of Rad59 that is distinct from that of Rad52.
###end p 65
###begin p 66
###xml 18 23 18 23 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rad59</italic>
###xml 129 133 129 133 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">RAD1</italic>
###xml 198 208 198 208 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rad59-Y92A</italic>
###xml 213 224 213 224 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rad59-K166A</italic>
###xml 240 241 240 241 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig4" ref-type="fig">4</xref>
###xml 243 244 243 244 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig8" ref-type="fig">8</xref>
###xml 252 256 252 256 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">RAD1</italic>
###xml 273 283 273 283 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rad59-Y92A</italic>
###xml 423 434 423 434 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rad59-K166A</italic>
###xml 492 496 492 496 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">RAD1</italic>
###xml 601 620 601 612 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rad1&#916;/rad1&#916;</italic>
###xml 681 685 673 677 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">RAD1</italic>
###xml 690 695 682 687 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">RAD59</italic>
###xml 874 878 866 870 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR46">2000</xref>
###xml 899 903 891 895 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR23">2009</xref>
###xml 920 924 912 916 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR25">2009</xref>
###xml 967 976 959 964 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">msh2&#916;</italic>
###xml 981 991 969 975 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rad59&#916;</italic>
###xml 1095 1096 1079 1080 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig9" ref-type="fig">9</xref>
###xml 1225 1229 1209 1213 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">MSH2</italic>
###xml 1262 1266 1246 1250 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">RAD1</italic>
###xml 1330 1335 1314 1319 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">RAD59</italic>
###xml 1352 1356 1336 1340 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR25">2009</xref>
Intriguingly, the rad59 missense alleles had reciprocal effects on translocation formation by SSA in the presence and absence of RAD1, which is revealed most clearly by comparing the effects of the rad59-Y92A and rad59-K166A alleles (Figs. 4, 8). When RAD1 is present, the rad59-Y92A allele results in a translocation frequency that is substantially higher than the frequency measured when it is absent, while, conversely, rad59-K166A confers considerably larger decreases in the presence of RAD1 than when it is absent. The differential ability of these alleles to suppress the defect exhibited in a rad1Delta/rad1Delta homozygote demonstrates a clear genetic interaction between RAD1 and RAD59 and suggests that Rad59 executes a function in support of Rad1-Rad10-mediated cleavage of non-homologous tails, perhaps in facilitating the binding of Msh2-Msh3 (Sugawara et al. 2000; Lyndaker and Alani 2009; Manthey et al. 2009). Examination of the relationship between msh2Delta and rad59Delta indicates that they are epistatic to one another, with respect to translocation formation by SSA (Fig. 9), which suggests that Msh2-Msh3 and Rad59 work together in this process. Furthermore, our group recently found that the loss of MSH2 suppresses the effect of losing RAD1 on translocation formation in much the same way as the loss of RAD59 (Manthey et al. 2009). This reinforces the notion that Rad59 and Msh2-Msh3 function together in supporting non-homologous tail cleavage by Rad1-Rad10.
###end p 66
###begin p 67
###xml 29 34 29 34 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rad59</italic>
###xml 232 237 232 237 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">RAD59</italic>
###xml 329 330 329 330 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig7" ref-type="fig">7</xref>
###xml 423 424 423 424 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig4" ref-type="fig">4</xref>
###xml 445 450 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 509 517 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">patients</span>
With the construction of the rad59 missense alleles described in this manuscript, we have acquired a better set of tools for dissecting how Rad59 supports SSA and determines the fate of broken chromosomes. The fact that the loss of RAD59 only minimally affects the viability of the cells following acute radiation exposure (Fig. 7), but clearly changes the pattern of repair following the generation of multiple DSBs (Fig. 4) suggests that if a human ortholog can be identified, attenuating its expression in patients undergoing radiation therapy might be of clinical utility. Cell killing, and therefore efficacy of treatment, should be unaffected, but loss of heterozygosity events due to SSA-driven genome rearrangements should be reduced, perhaps minimizing the incidence of secondary cancers.
###end p 67
